  <COMMENT line1="300" col1="1" line2="300" col2="69" start="44701" end="44769">#' Accessor functions for the normalization factors in a DESeqDataSet</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="301" col1="1" line2="301" col2="10" start="44850" end="44859">#' object.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="302" col1="1" line2="302" col2="2" start="44999" end="45000">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="303" col1="1" line2="303" col2="83" start="45148" end="45230">#' Gene-specific normalization factors for each sample can be provided as a matrix,</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="304" col1="1" line2="304" col2="85" start="45297" end="45381">#' which will preempt \code{\link{sizeFactors}}. In some experiments, counts for each</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="305" col1="1" line2="305" col2="82" start="45446" end="45527">#' sample have varying dependence on covariates, e.g. on GC-content for sequencing</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="306" col1="1" line2="306" col2="73" start="45595" end="45667">#' data run on different days, and in this case it makes sense to provide</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="307" col1="1" line2="307" col2="74" start="45744" end="45817">#' gene-specific factors for each sample rather than a single size factor.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="308" col1="1" line2="308" col2="2" start="45893" end="45894">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="309" col1="1" line2="309" col2="89" start="46042" end="46130">#' Normalization factors alter the model of \code{\link{DESeq}} in the following way, for</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="310" col1="1" line2="310" col2="100" start="46191" end="46290">#' counts \eqn{K_{ij}}{K_ij} and normalization factors \eqn{NF_{ij}}{NF_ij} for gene i and sample j:</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="311" col1="1" line2="311" col2="2" start="46340" end="46341">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="312" col1="1" line2="312" col2="85" start="46489" end="46573">#' \deqn{ K_{ij} \sim \textrm{NB}( \mu_{ij}, \alpha_i) }{ K_ij ~ NB(mu_ij, alpha_i) }</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="313" col1="1" line2="313" col2="59" start="46638" end="46696">#' \deqn{ \mu_{ij} = NF_{ij} q_{ij} }{ mu_ij = NF_ij q_ij }</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="314" col1="1" line2="314" col2="2" start="46787" end="46788">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="315" col1="1" line2="315" col2="100" start="46936" end="47035">#' @note Normalization factors are on the scale of the counts (similar to \code{\link{sizeFactors}})</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="316" col1="1" line2="316" col2="101" start="47085" end="47185">#' and unlike offsets, which are typically on the scale of the predictors (in this case, log counts).</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="317" col1="1" line2="317" col2="84" start="47234" end="47317">#' Normalization factors should include library size normalization. They should have</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="318" col1="1" line2="318" col2="101" start="47383" end="47483">#' row-wise geometric mean near 1, as is the case with size factors, such that the mean of normalized</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="319" col1="1" line2="319" col2="78" start="47532" end="47609">#' counts is close to the mean of unnormalized counts. See example code below.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="320" col1="1" line2="320" col2="2" start="47681" end="47682">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="321" col1="1" line2="321" col2="19" start="47830" end="47848">#' @docType methods</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="322" col1="1" line2="322" col2="29" start="47979" end="48007">#' @name normalizationFactors</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="323" col1="1" line2="323" col2="31" start="48128" end="48158">#' @rdname normalizationFactors</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="324" col1="1" line2="324" col2="123" start="48277" end="48399">#' @aliases normalizationFactors normalizationFactors,DESeqDataSet-method normalizationFactors&lt;-,DESeqDataSet,matrix-method</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="325" col1="1" line2="325" col2="46" start="48426" end="48471">#' @param object a \code{DESeqDataSet} object.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="326" col1="1" line2="326" col2="51" start="48575" end="48625">#' @param value the matrix of normalization factors</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="327" col1="1" line2="327" col2="34" start="48724" end="48757">#' @param ... additional arguments</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="328" col1="1" line2="328" col2="12" start="48873" end="48884">#' @examples</COMMENT>

  <COMMENT line1="330" col1="1" line2="330" col2="45" start="49171" end="49215">#' dds &lt;- makeExampleDESeqDataSet(n=100, m=4)</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="331" col1="1" line2="331" col2="2" start="49320" end="49321">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="332" col1="1" line2="332" col2="60" start="49469" end="49528">#' normFactors &lt;- matrix(runif(nrow(dds)*ncol(dds),0.5,1.5),</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="333" col1="1" line2="333" col2="55" start="49618" end="49672">#'                       ncol=ncol(dds),nrow=nrow(dds),</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="334" col1="1" line2="334" col2="64" start="49767" end="49830">#'                       dimnames=list(1:nrow(dds),1:ncol(dds)))</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="335" col1="1" line2="335" col2="2" start="49916" end="49917">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="336" col1="1" line2="336" col2="63" start="50065" end="50127">#' # the normalization factors matrix should not have 0's in it</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="337" col1="1" line2="337" col2="54" start="50214" end="50267">#' # it should have geometric mean near 1 for each row</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="338" col1="1" line2="338" col2="63" start="50363" end="50425">#' normFactors &lt;- normFactors / exp(rowMeans(log(normFactors)))</COMMENT>

  <COMMENT line1="412" col1="1" line2="412" col2="61" start="61389" end="61449">#' Estimate the size factors for a \code{\link{DESeqDataSet}}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="413" col1="1" line2="413" col2="3" start="61538" end="61540">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="414" col1="1" line2="414" col2="53" start="61687" end="61739">#' This function estimates the size factors using the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="415" col1="1" line2="415" col2="76" start="61836" end="61911">#' "median ratio method" described by Equation 5 in Anders and Huber (2010).</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="416" col1="1" line2="416" col2="100" start="61985" end="62084">#' The estimated size factors can be accessed using the accessor function \code{\link{sizeFactors}}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="417" col1="1" line2="417" col2="59" start="62134" end="62192">#' Alternative library size estimators can also be supplied</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="418" col1="1" line2="418" col2="61" start="62283" end="62343">#' using the assignment function \code{\link{sizeFactors&lt;-}}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="419" col1="1" line2="419" col2="3" start="62432" end="62434">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="420" col1="1" line2="420" col2="52" start="62581" end="62632">#' Typically, the function is called with the idiom:</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="421" col1="1" line2="421" col2="2" start="62730" end="62731">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="422" col1="1" line2="422" col2="41" start="62879" end="62919">#' \code{dds &lt;- estimateSizeFactors(dds)}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="423" col1="1" line2="423" col2="2" start="63028" end="63029">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="424" col1="1" line2="424" col2="83" start="63177" end="63259">#' See \code{\link{DESeq}} for a description of the use of size factors in the GLM.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="425" col1="1" line2="425" col2="65" start="63326" end="63390">#' One should call this function after \code{\link{DESeqDataSet}}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="426" col1="1" line2="426" col2="77" start="63475" end="63551">#' unless size factors are manually specified with \code{\link{sizeFactors}}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="427" col1="1" line2="427" col2="91" start="63624" end="63714">#' Alternatively, gene-specific normalization factors for each sample can be provided using</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="428" col1="1" line2="428" col2="89" start="63773" end="63861">#' \code{\link{normalizationFactors}} which will always preempt \code{\link{sizeFactors}}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="429" col1="1" line2="429" col2="19" start="63922" end="63940">#' in calculations.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="430" col1="1" line2="430" col2="2" start="64071" end="64072">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="431" col1="1" line2="431" col2="78" start="64220" end="64297">#' Internally, the function calls \code{\link{estimateSizeFactorsForMatrix}}, </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="432" col1="1" line2="432" col2="50" start="64369" end="64418">#' which provides more details on the calculation.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="433" col1="1" line2="433" col2="2" start="64518" end="64519">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="434" col1="1" line2="434" col2="30" start="64667" end="64696">#' @rdname estimateSizeFactors</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="435" col1="1" line2="435" col2="3" start="64816" end="64818">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="436" col1="1" line2="436" col2="31" start="64965" end="64995">#' @param object a DESeqDataSet</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="437" col1="1" line2="437" col2="80" start="65114" end="65193">#' @param type Method for estimation: either "ratio", "poscounts", or "iterate".</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="438" col1="1" line2="438" col2="92" start="65263" end="65354">#' "ratio" uses the standard median ratio method introduced in DESeq. The size factor is the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="439" col1="1" line2="439" col2="86" start="65412" end="65497">#' median ratio of the sample over a "pseudosample": for each gene, the geometric mean</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="440" col1="1" line2="440" col2="18" start="65561" end="65578">#' of all samples.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="441" col1="1" line2="441" col2="71" start="65710" end="65780">#' "poscounts" and "iterate" offer alternative estimators, which can be</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="442" col1="1" line2="442" col2="75" start="65859" end="65933">#' used even when all genes contain a sample with a zero (a problem for the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="443" col1="1" line2="443" col2="80" start="66008" end="66087">#' default method, as the geometric mean becomes zero, and the ratio undefined).</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="444" col1="1" line2="444" col2="80" start="66157" end="66236">#' The "poscounts" estimator deals with a gene with some zeros, by calculating a</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="445" col1="1" line2="445" col2="89" start="66306" end="66394">#' modified geometric mean by taking the n-th root of the product of the non-zero counts.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="446" col1="1" line2="446" col2="95" start="66455" end="66549">#' This evolved out of use cases with Paul McMurdie's phyloseq package for metagenomic samples.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="447" col1="1" line2="447" col2="94" start="66604" end="66697">#' The "iterate" estimator iterates between estimating the dispersion with a design of ~1, and</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="448" col1="1" line2="448" col2="72" start="66753" end="66824">#' finding a size factor vector by numerically optimizing the likelihood</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="449" col1="1" line2="449" col2="19" start="66902" end="66920">#' of the ~1 model.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="450" col1="1" line2="450" col2="80" start="67051" end="67130">#' @param locfunc a function to compute a location for a sample. By default, the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="451" col1="1" line2="451" col2="58" start="67200" end="67257">#' median is used. However, especially for low counts, the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="452" col1="1" line2="452" col2="97" start="67349" end="67445">#' \code{\link[genefilter]{shorth}} function from the genefilter package may give better results.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="453" col1="1" line2="453" col2="58" start="67498" end="67555">#' @param geoMeans by default this is not provided and the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="454" col1="1" line2="454" col2="68" start="67647" end="67714">#' geometric means of the counts are calculated within the function.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="455" col1="1" line2="455" col2="72" start="67796" end="67867">#' A vector of geometric means from another count matrix can be provided</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="456" col1="1" line2="456" col2="68" start="67945" end="68012">#' for a "frozen" size factor calculation. The size factors will be </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="457" col1="1" line2="457" col2="71" start="68094" end="68164">#' scaled to have a geometric mean of 1 when supplying \code{geoMeans}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="458" col1="1" line2="458" col2="90" start="68243" end="68332">#' @param controlGenes optional, numeric or logical index vector specifying those genes to</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="459" col1="1" line2="459" col2="71" start="68392" end="68462">#' use for size factor estimation (e.g. housekeeping or spike-in genes)</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="460" col1="1" line2="460" col2="81" start="68541" end="68621">#' @param normMatrix optional, a matrix of normalization factors which do not yet</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="461" col1="1" line2="461" col2="76" start="68690" end="68765">#' control for library size. Note that this argument should not be used (and</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="462" col1="1" line2="462" col2="79" start="68839" end="68917">#' will be ignored) if the \code{dds} object was created using \code{tximport}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="463" col1="1" line2="463" col2="71" start="68988" end="69058">#' In this case, the information in \code{assays(dds)[["avgTxLength"]]}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="464" col1="1" line2="464" col2="69" start="69137" end="69205">#' is automatically used to create appropriate normalization factors.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="465" col1="1" line2="465" col2="64" start="69286" end="69349">#' Providing \code{normMatrix} will estimate size factors on the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="466" col1="1" line2="466" col2="73" start="69435" end="69507">#' count matrix divided by \code{normMatrix} and store the product of the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="467" col1="1" line2="467" col2="76" start="69584" end="69659">#' size factors and \code{normMatrix} as \code{\link{normalizationFactors}}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="468" col1="1" line2="468" col2="65" start="69733" end="69797">#' It is recommended to divide out the row-wise geometric mean of</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="469" col1="1" line2="469" col2="59" start="69882" end="69940">#' \code{normMatrix} so the rows roughly are centered on 1.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="470" col1="1" line2="470" col2="41" start="70031" end="70071">#' @param quiet whether to print messages</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="471" col1="1" line2="471" col2="3" start="70180" end="70182">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="472" col1="1" line2="472" col2="78" start="70329" end="70406">#' @return The DESeqDataSet passed as parameters, with the size factors filled</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="473" col1="1" line2="473" col2="6" start="70478" end="70483">#' in.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="474" col1="1" line2="474" col2="23" start="70627" end="70649">#' @author Simon Anders</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="475" col1="1" line2="475" col2="54" start="70776" end="70829">#' @seealso \code{\link{estimateSizeFactorsForMatrix}}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="476" col1="1" line2="476" col2="2" start="70925" end="70926">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="477" col1="1" line2="477" col2="14" start="71074" end="71087">#' @references</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="478" col1="1" line2="478" col2="2" start="71223" end="71224">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="479" col1="1" line2="479" col2="41" start="71372" end="71412">#' Reference for the median ratio method:</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="480" col1="1" line2="480" col2="3" start="71521" end="71523">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="481" col1="1" line2="481" col2="90" start="71670" end="71759">#' Simon Anders, Wolfgang Huber: Differential expression analysis for sequence count data.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="482" col1="1" line2="482" col2="82" start="71819" end="71900">#' Genome Biology 2010, 11:106. \url{http://dx.doi.org/10.1186/gb-2010-11-10-r106}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="483" col1="1" line2="483" col2="3" start="71968" end="71970">#' </COMMENT>

          </expr>
        </expr>
        <expr line1="587" col1="3" line2="595" col2="3" start="87466" end="88658">
          <IF line1="587" col1="3" line2="587" col2="4" start="87466" end="87467">if</IF>
          <OP-LEFT-PAREN line1="587" col1="6" line2="587" col2="6" start="87469" end="87469">(</OP-LEFT-PAREN>
          <expr line1="587" col1="7" line2="587" col2="12" start="87470" end="87475">

          </expr>
          <OP-RIGHT-PAREN line1="587" col1="13" line2="587" col2="13" start="87476" end="87476">)</OP-RIGHT-PAREN>
          <expr line1="587" col1="15" line2="595" col2="3" start="87478" end="88658">
            <OP-LEFT-BRACE line1="587" col1="15" line2="587" col2="15" start="87478" end="87478">{</OP-LEFT-BRACE>
            <expr line1="588" col1="5" line2="594" col2="2" start="87617" end="88508">
              <expr line1="588" col1="5" line2="588" col2="8" start="87617" end="87620">
                <SYMBOL_FUNCTION_CALL line1="588" col1="5" line2="588" col2="8" start="87617" end="87620">stop</SYMBOL_FUNCTION_CALL>
              </expr>
              <OP-LEFT-PAREN line1="588" col1="9" line2="588" col2="9" start="87621" end="87621">(</OP-LEFT-PAREN>
              <expr line1="588" col1="10" line2="594" col2="1" start="87622" end="88507">
                <STR_CONST line1="588" col1="10" line2="594" col2="1" start="87622" end="88507">"

  The design matrix has the same number of samples and coefficients to fit,
  so estimation of dispersion is not possible. Treating samples
  as replicates was deprecated in v1.20 and no longer supported since v1.22.

              </expr>
              <OP-RIGHT-PAREN line1="594" col1="2" line2="594" col2="2" start="88508" end="88508">)</OP-RIGHT-PAREN>

  <COMMENT line1="599" col1="1" line2="599" col2="46" start="89252" end="89297">#' Estimate the dispersions for a DESeqDataSet</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="600" col1="1" line2="600" col2="3" start="89401" end="89403">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="601" col1="1" line2="601" col2="85" start="89550" end="89634">#' This function obtains dispersion estimates for Negative Binomial distributed data.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="602" col1="1" line2="602" col2="2" start="89699" end="89700">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="603" col1="1" line2="603" col2="51" start="89848" end="89898">#' Typically the function is called with the idiom:</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="604" col1="1" line2="604" col2="2" start="89997" end="89998">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="605" col1="1" line2="605" col2="41" start="90146" end="90186">#' \code{dds &lt;- estimateDispersions(dds)}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="606" col1="1" line2="606" col2="2" start="90295" end="90296">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="607" col1="1" line2="607" col2="80" start="90444" end="90523">#' The fitting proceeds as follows: for each gene, an estimate of the dispersion</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="608" col1="1" line2="608" col2="68" start="90593" end="90660">#' is found which maximizes the Cox Reid-adjusted profile likelihood</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="609" col1="1" line2="609" col2="72" start="90742" end="90813">#' (the methods of Cox Reid-adjusted profile likelihood maximization for</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="610" col1="1" line2="610" col2="71" start="90891" end="90961">#' estimation of dispersion in RNA-Seq data were developed by McCarthy,</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="611" col1="1" line2="611" col2="66" start="91040" end="91105">#' et al. (2012), first implemented in the edgeR package in 2010);</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="612" col1="1" line2="612" col2="102" start="91189" end="91290">#' a trend line capturing the dispersion-mean relationship is fit to the maximum likelihood estimates;</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="613" col1="1" line2="613" col2="73" start="91338" end="91410">#' a normal prior is determined for the log dispersion estimates centered</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="614" col1="1" line2="614" col2="46" start="91487" end="91532">#' on the predicted value from the trended fit</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="615" col1="1" line2="615" col2="77" start="91636" end="91712">#' with variance equal to the difference between the observed variance of the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="616" col1="1" line2="616" col2="63" start="91785" end="91847">#' log dispersion estimates and the expected sampling variance;</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="617" col1="1" line2="617" col2="66" start="91934" end="91999">#' finally maximum a posteriori dispersion estimates are returned.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="618" col1="1" line2="618" col2="63" start="92083" end="92145">#' This final dispersion parameter is used in subsequent tests.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="619" col1="1" line2="619" col2="97" start="92232" end="92328">#' The final dispersion estimates can be accessed from an object using \code{\link{dispersions}}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="620" col1="1" line2="620" col2="58" start="92381" end="92438">#' The fitted dispersion-mean relationship is also used in</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="621" col1="1" line2="621" col2="51" start="92530" end="92580">#' \code{\link{varianceStabilizingTransformation}}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="622" col1="1" line2="622" col2="84" start="92679" end="92762">#' All of the intermediate values (gene-wise dispersion estimates, fitted dispersion</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="623" col1="1" line2="623" col2="78" start="92828" end="92905">#' estimates from the trended fit, etc.) are stored in \code{mcols(dds)}, with</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="624" col1="1" line2="624" col2="63" start="92977" end="93039">#' information about these columns in \code{mcols(mcols(dds))}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="625" col1="1" line2="625" col2="2" start="93126" end="93127">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="626" col1="1" line2="626" col2="69" start="93275" end="93343">#' The log normal prior on the dispersion parameter has been proposed</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="627" col1="1" line2="627" col2="67" start="93424" end="93490">#' by Wu, et al. (2012) and is also implemented in the DSS package.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="628" col1="1" line2="628" col2="2" start="93573" end="93574">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="629" col1="1" line2="629" col2="78" start="93722" end="93799">#' In DESeq2, the dispersion estimation procedure described above replaces the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="630" col1="1" line2="630" col2="82" start="93871" end="93952">#' different methods of dispersion from the previous version of the DESeq package.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="631" col1="1" line2="631" col2="3" start="94020" end="94022">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="632" col1="1" line2="632" col2="94" start="94169" end="94262">#' Since version 1.29, DESeq2 can call the glmGamPoi package, which can speed up the inference</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="633" col1="1" line2="633" col2="92" start="94318" end="94409">#' and is optimized for fitting many samles with very small counts (for example single cell </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="634" col1="1" line2="634" col2="94" start="94467" end="94560">#' RNA-seq data). To call functions from the glmGamPoi package, make sure that it is installed</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="635" col1="1" line2="635" col2="99" start="94616" end="94714">#' and set \code{fitType = "glmGamPoi"}. In addition, to the gene estimates, the trend and the MAP,</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="636" col1="1" line2="636" col2="94" start="94765" end="94858">#' the glmGamPoi package calculates the corresponding quasi-likelihood estimates. Those can be</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="637" col1="1" line2="637" col2="79" start="94914" end="94992">#' used with the \code{nbinomLRT()} test to get more precise p-value estimates.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="638" col1="1" line2="638" col2="2" start="95063" end="95064">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="639" col1="1" line2="639" col2="70" start="95212" end="95281">#' The lower-level functions called by \code{estimateDispersions} are:</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="640" col1="1" line2="640" col2="44" start="95361" end="95404">#' \code{\link{estimateDispersionsGeneEst}},</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="641" col1="1" line2="641" col2="44" start="95510" end="95553">#' \code{\link{estimateDispersionsFit}}, and</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="642" col1="1" line2="642" col2="40" start="95659" end="95698">#' \code{\link{estimateDispersionsMAP}}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="643" col1="1" line2="643" col2="3" start="95808" end="95810">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="644" col1="1" line2="644" col2="30" start="95957" end="95986">#' @rdname estimateDispersions</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="645" col1="1" line2="645" col2="2" start="96106" end="96107">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="646" col1="1" line2="646" col2="31" start="96255" end="96285">#' @param object a DESeqDataSet</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="647" col1="1" line2="647" col2="70" start="96404" end="96473">#' @param fitType either "parametric", "local", "mean", or "glmGamPoi"</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="648" col1="1" line2="648" col2="64" start="96553" end="96616">#' for the type of fitting of dispersions to the mean intensity.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="649" col1="1" line2="649" col2="12" start="96702" end="96713">#' \itemize{</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="650" col1="1" line2="650" col2="67" start="96851" end="96917">#'   \item parametric - fit a dispersion-mean relation of the form:</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="651" col1="1" line2="651" col2="56" start="97000" end="97055">#'     \deqn{dispersion = asymptDisp + extraPois / mean}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="652" col1="1" line2="652" col2="93" start="97149" end="97241">#'     via a robust gamma-family GLM. The coefficients \code{asymptDisp} and \code{extraPois}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="653" col1="1" line2="653" col2="93" start="97298" end="97390">#'     are given in the attribute \code{coefficients} of the \code{\link{dispersionFunction}}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="654" col1="1" line2="654" col2="21" start="97447" end="97467">#'     of the object.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="655" col1="1" line2="655" col2="67" start="97596" end="97662">#'   \item local - use the locfit package to fit a local regression</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="656" col1="1" line2="656" col2="80" start="97745" end="97824">#'     of log dispersions over log base mean (normal scale means and dispersions</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="657" col1="1" line2="657" col2="77" start="97894" end="97970">#'     are input and output for \code{\link{dispersionFunction}}). The points</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="658" col1="1" line2="658" col2="69" start="98043" end="98111">#'     are weighted by normalized mean count in the local regression.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="659" col1="1" line2="659" col2="65" start="98192" end="98256">#'   \item mean - use the mean of gene-wise dispersion estimates.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="660" col1="1" line2="660" col2="91" start="98341" end="98431">#'   \item glmGamPoi - use the glmGamPoi package to fit the gene-wise dispersion, its trend</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="661" col1="1" line2="661" col2="83" start="98490" end="98572">#'     and calculate the MAP based on the quasi-likelihood framework. The trend is </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="662" col1="1" line2="662" col2="50" start="98639" end="98688">#'     calculated using a local median regression.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="663" col1="1" line2="663" col2="4" start="98788" end="98791">#' }</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="664" col1="1" line2="664" col2="88" start="98937" end="99024">#' @param maxit control parameter: maximum number of iterations to allow for convergence</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="665" col1="1" line2="665" col2="78" start="99086" end="99163">#' @param useCR whether to use Cox-Reid correction - see McCarthy et al (2012)</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="666" col1="1" line2="666" col2="84" start="99235" end="99318">#' @param weightThreshold threshold for subsetting the design matrix and GLM weights</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="667" col1="1" line2="667" col2="42" start="99384" end="99425">#' for calculating the Cox-Reid correction</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="668" col1="1" line2="668" col2="54" start="99533" end="99586">#' @param quiet whether to print messages at each step</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="669" col1="1" line2="669" col2="92" start="99682" end="99773">#' @param modelMatrix an optional matrix which will be used for fitting the expected counts.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="670" col1="1" line2="670" col2="73" start="99831" end="99903">#' by default, the model matrix is constructed from \code{design(object)}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="671" col1="1" line2="671" col2="83" start="99980" end="100062">#' @param minmu lower bound on the estimated count for fitting gene-wise dispersion</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="672" col1="1" line2="672" col2="2" start="100129" end="100130">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="673" col1="1" line2="673" col2="81" start="100278" end="100358">#' @return The DESeqDataSet passed as parameters, with the dispersion information</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="674" col1="1" line2="674" col2="87" start="100427" end="100513">#' filled in as metadata columns, accessible via \code{mcols}, or the final dispersions</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="675" col1="1" line2="675" col2="44" start="100576" end="100619">#' accessible via \code{\link{dispersions}}.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="676" col1="1" line2="676" col2="2" start="100725" end="100726">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="677" col1="1" line2="677" col2="24" start="100874" end="100897">#' @references \itemize{</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="678" col1="1" line2="678" col2="98" start="101023" end="101120">#'   \item Simon Anders, Wolfgang Huber: Differential expression analysis for sequence count data.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="679" col1="1" line2="679" col2="84" start="101172" end="101255">#' Genome Biology 11 (2010) R106, \url{http://dx.doi.org/10.1186/gb-2010-11-10-r106}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="680" col1="1" line2="680" col2="100" start="101321" end="101420">#'   \item McCarthy, DJ, Chen, Y, Smyth, GK: Differential expression analysis of multifactor RNA-Seq</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="681" col1="1" line2="681" col2="97" start="101470" end="101566">#' experiments with respect to biological variation. Nucleic Acids Research 40 (2012), 4288-4297,</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="682" col1="1" line2="682" col2="45" start="101619" end="101663">#' \url{http://dx.doi.org/10.1093/nar/gks042}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="683" col1="1" line2="683" col2="99" start="101768" end="101866">#'   \item Wu, H., Wang, C. &amp; Wu, Z. A new shrinkage estimator for dispersion improves differential</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="684" col1="1" line2="684" col2="62" start="101917" end="101978">#' expression detection in RNA-seq data. Biostatistics (2012).</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="685" col1="1" line2="685" col2="55" start="102066" end="102120">#' \url{http://dx.doi.org/10.1093/biostatistics/kxs033}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="686" col1="1" line2="686" col2="148" start="102215" end="102362">#'   \item Ahlmann-Eltze, C., Huber, W. glmGamPoi: Fitting Gamma-Poisson Generalized Linear Models on Single Cell Count Data. Bioinformatics (2020).</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="687" col1="1" line2="687" col2="56" start="102364" end="102419">#' \url{https://doi.org/10.1093/bioinformatics/btaa1009}</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="688" col1="1" line2="688" col2="4" start="102513" end="102516">#' }</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="689" col1="1" line2="689" col2="2" start="102662" end="102663">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="690" col1="1" line2="690" col2="12" start="102811" end="102822">#' @examples</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="691" col1="1" line2="691" col2="3" start="102960" end="102962">#' </COMMENT>

  <COMMENT line1="702" col1="1" line2="702" col2="39" start="104599" end="104637">#' Show method for DESeqResults objects</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="703" col1="1" line2="703" col2="2" start="104748" end="104749">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="704" col1="1" line2="704" col2="55" start="104897" end="104951">#' Prints out the information from the metadata columns</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="705" col1="1" line2="705" col2="56" start="105046" end="105101">#' of the results object regarding the log2 fold changes</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="706" col1="1" line2="706" col2="51" start="105195" end="105245">#' and p-values, then shows the DataFrame using the</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="707" col1="1" line2="707" col2="19" start="105344" end="105362">#' standard method.</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="708" col1="1" line2="708" col2="3" start="105493" end="105495">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="709" col1="1" line2="709" col2="15" start="105642" end="105656">#' @rdname show</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="710" col1="1" line2="710" col2="2" start="105791" end="105792">#'</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="711" col1="1" line2="711" col2="23" start="105940" end="105962">#' @author Michael Love</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="712" col1="1" line2="712" col2="3" start="106089" end="106091">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="713" col1="1" line2="713" col2="38" start="106238" end="106275">#' @param object a DESeqResults object</COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="714" col1="1" line2="714" col2="3" start="106387" end="106389">#' </COMMENT>
  <COMMENT line1="715" col1="1" line2="715" col2="10" start="106536" end="106545">#' @export</COMMENT>
  <expr line1="716" col1="1" line2="720" col2="2" start="106685" end="107282">
    <expr line1="716" col1="1" line2="716" col2="9" start="106685" end="106693">
      <SYMBOL_FUNCTION_CALL line1="716" col1="1" line2="716" col2="9" start="106685" end="106693">setMethod</SYMBOL_FUNCTION_CALL>
